<p><i><b>Graduation</b></i> is the third <a href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album" class="mw-redirect">studio album</a> by American <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> artist <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>, it was released on September 11, 2007 on <a href="/wiki/Roc-A-Fella_Records" title="Roc-A-Fella Records">Roc-A-Fella Records</a>. Recording sessions for the album took place during 2005 to 2007 at <a href="/wiki/Chung_King_Studios" title="Chung King Studios">Chung King Studios</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Studios" title="Sony Music Studios">Sony Music Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and at <a href="/wiki/Chalice_Recording_Studios" title="Chalice Recording Studios">Chalice Studios</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Record_Plant" title="The Record Plant" class="mw-redirect">The Record Plant</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>. It was primarily produced by West and <a href="/wiki/DJ_Toomp" title="DJ Toomp">DJ Toomp</a>, and features guest contributions from artists including <a href="/wiki/Mos_Def" title="Mos Def">Mos Def</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dwele" title="Dwele">Dwele</a>, <a href="/wiki/T-Pain" title="T-Pain">T-Pain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Martin" title="Chris Martin">Chris Martin</a> of <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a>. The album's cover artwork was designed by Japanese contemporary artist <a href="/wiki/Takashi_Murakami" title="Takashi Murakami">Takashi Murakami</a>.</p>
<p>Inspired by Irish rock band <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> and other musical groups to make more inspirational, anthemic hip-hop music, West incorporated <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synthesizer</a> sounds into his production and dabbled with <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic music</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Sample_(music)" title="Sample (music)" class="mw-redirect">sampling</a> a wider spectrum of musical genres. Lyrically, <i>Graduation</i> is more introspective in comparison to its predecessors, as West dedicated much of the album towards analyzing himself and conveying his ambivalent outlook on his newfound fame. It continues the education theme of West's previous two studio albums, <i><a href="/wiki/The_College_Dropout" title="The College Dropout">The College Dropout</a></i> (2004) and <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Registration" title="Late Registration">Late Registration</a></i> (2005).</p>
<p>The album debuted at number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, selling 957,000 copies in its first week. It produced five singles, including international hits "<a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Tell_Me_Nothing" title="Can't Tell Me Nothing">Can't Tell Me Nothing</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Stronger_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Stronger (Kanye West song)">Stronger</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Good_Life_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Good Life (Kanye West song)">Good Life</a>." The coinciding release dates of <i>Graduation</i> and rapper <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Curtis_(50_Cent_album)" title="Curtis (50 Cent album)">Curtis</a></i> generated much publicity over the idea of a sales competition, resulting in record-breaking sales performances by both albums. <i>Graduation</i> received mostly positive reviews from most music critics and earned West several accolades, including a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Grammy Award for Best Rap Album</a>. The album has sold 2,700,000 copies in the US and has been certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">double platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Graduation</i> is the third installment of Kanye West's planned <a href="/wiki/Tetralogy" title="Tetralogy">tetralogy</a> of education-themed studio albums, which West subsequently deviated from due to the events surrounding the conception of his fourth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/808s_%26_Heartbreak" title="808s &amp; Heartbreak">808s &amp; Heartbreak</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ODB_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODB-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> The album demonstrates yet another distinctive evolution in West's musical style and approach to production. After spending the previous year touring the world with Irish rock band <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> on their <a href="/wiki/Vertigo_Tour" title="Vertigo Tour">Vertigo Tour</a>, West felt inspired by watching <a href="/wiki/Bono" title="Bono">Bono</a> open stadium tours every night to incredible ovations and sought out to compose anthemic rap songs that could operate more efficiently in large arenas.<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> In his attempt to accomplish this "stadium-status" endeavor, West incorporated electronic <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synthesizers</a> into his <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_production" title="Hip hop production">hip-hop production</a>, which also finds him experimenting with <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic music</a> and being influenced by <a href="/wiki/1980s_in_music" title="1980s in music">music of the 1980s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Loop_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Loop-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stoppelenburg_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stoppelenburg-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> West was particularly influenced by <a href="/wiki/House_music" title="House music">house music</a>, a subgenre of <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">electronic dance music</a> that first originated in his hometown of <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a> in the early 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-Park_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Park-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> In the past, West has stated that while growing up, he would listen to hip-hop music at home or in his car, but when he felt like dancing, he would attend a house club.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>West further broadened his musical palette by not limiting himself to his customary <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> samples, and instead sampled from a more eclectic variety of musical genres, including <a href="/wiki/Euro_disco" title="Euro disco">euro-disco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hard_rock" title="Hard rock">hard rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronica" title="Electronica">electronica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lounge_music" title="Lounge music">lounge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Synthpop" title="Synthpop">synth-pop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electro_(music)" title="Electro (music)">electro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dub_(music)" title="Dub (music)">dub</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cowie_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cowie-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> For much of the album, West adopted a dilatory, exuberant <a href="/wiki/Rapping" title="Rapping">rapping</a> delivery in emulation of Bono's operatic vocal stylings.<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to U2, West drew inspiration from <a href="/wiki/Arena_rock" title="Arena rock">arena rock</a> bands such as <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a> for <a href="/wiki/Melody" title="Melody">melody</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chord_progression" title="Chord progression">chord progression</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Loop_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Loop-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Serwer_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Serwer-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> In terms of lyricism, West sought out to simplify some of his rhymes after touring with The Rolling Stones on their <a href="/wiki/A_Bigger_Bang_(concert_tour)" title="A Bigger Bang (concert tour)">A Bigger Bang</a> concert tour and discovering that he could not electrify the audience as well with his most complex lyrical themes.<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording">Recording</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Recording">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U2_brussels_fly_2005-10-06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/U2_brussels_fly_2005-10-06.jpg/250px-U2_brussels_fly_2005-10-06.jpg" width="250" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/U2_brussels_fly_2005-10-06.jpg/375px-U2_brussels_fly_2005-10-06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/U2_brussels_fly_2005-10-06.jpg/500px-U2_brussels_fly_2005-10-06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="473" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:U2_brussels_fly_2005-10-06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf6/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
West's experiences on arena rock tours such as U2's Vertigo Tour (pictured) inspired his direction for the album.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Kanye West began working on <i>Graduation</i> immediately after releasing his second studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Registration" title="Late Registration">Late Registration</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Staff_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Staff-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> By late September of 2005, West had already completed three songs for the album, which he intended to contain a total of twelve tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-Staff_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Staff-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Around the time of the recording of the third studio album, West listened to songs written by <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country</a> singer-songwriters <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Cash" title="Johnny Cash">Johnny Cash</a> in hopes of developing methods to augment his wordplay and story-telling ability. The former musician had been recommended to West by multiple of his friends, including English disc jockey <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Ronson" title="Samantha Ronson">Samantha Ronson</a>, all of whom claimed his music and the way he dealt with the press reminded them of Dylan. West also listened to his most favorite <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative rock</a> bands, including <a href="/wiki/The_Killers" title="The Killers">The Killers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radiohead" title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Modest_Mouse" title="Modest Mouse">Modest Mouse</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Keane_(band)" title="Keane (band)">Keane</a>, in order to gain ideas on how to make his hip-hop production more stadium-friendly.<sup id="cite_ref-Praise_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Praise-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In comparison to previous albums, <i>Graduation</i> features fewer guest appearances from other recording artists. West elaborated that it was a fully conscious decision to keep his guest vocalists to a minimum, saying that, "When I hear the records of my favorite bands — The Killers or <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a> — you only hear one voice from start to finish."<sup id="cite_ref-GradDay_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradDay-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> singers <a href="/wiki/T-Pain" title="T-Pain">T-Pain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dwele" title="Dwele">Dwele</a>, New York rappers <a href="/wiki/Mos_Def" title="Mos Def">Mos Def</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albert_Daniels" title="Albert Daniels">ALBe. Back</a>, and famed hip-hop record producer <a href="/wiki/DJ_Premier" title="DJ Premier">DJ Premier</a> are featured within individual tracks primarily to deliver <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hooks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Refrain" title="Refrain">choruses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rabin_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rabin-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> However, though he originally intended for <i>Graduation</i> to be completely devoid of guest rap verses, West later decided to invite <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a> on the track "Barry Bonds."<sup id="cite_ref-BarryBonds_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BarryBonds-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> At the time, the two MCs had been working together, with West contributing to the production of Lil Wayne's sixth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Tha_Carter_III" title="Tha Carter III">Tha Carter III</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Many songs on <i>Graduation</i> contain background vocals provided by <a href="/wiki/Connie_Mitchell" title="Connie Mitchell">Connie Mitchell</a> of the Australian <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">dance music</a> group <a href="/wiki/Sneaky_Sound_System" title="Sneaky Sound System">Sneaky Sound System</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-linernotes_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linernotes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The collaboration came about when West met her bandmates Angus McDonald and Daimon Downey at a diner in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a> while touring the country with <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> around November of 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-Nui_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nui-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-conniemitch_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conniemitch-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Seeking musical inspiration, West asked McDonald for ideas, who suggested that he be introduced to Mitchell.<sup id="cite_ref-conniemitch_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conniemitch-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon meeting Mitchell after she arrived at <a href="/wiki/Studios_301" title="Studios 301">Studios 301</a> where he was recording music during the tour, West had her sing over a vocal track and quickly took a liking to her voice.<sup id="cite_ref-Nui_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nui-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-conniemitch_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conniemitch-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> U2 singer <a href="/wiki/Bono" title="Bono">Bono</a> and guitarist <a href="/wiki/The_Edge" title="The Edge">The Edge</a> also complimented Mitchell's singing while stopping by the studio.<sup id="cite_ref-conniemitch_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conniemitch-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Some time later, Mitchell received a call from West, who asked her to travel to <a href="/wiki/The_Record_Plant" title="The Record Plant" class="mw-redirect">The Record Plant</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> to begin recording tracks for his third studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-conniemitch_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conniemitch-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Mitchell later admitted that while she previously didn't know who Kanye West was and never really cared for hip-hop music, the collaboration has changed her views.<sup id="cite_ref-Nui_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nui-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ConnieMitchellTheVoice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bd/ConnieMitchellTheVoice.jpg/210px-ConnieMitchellTheVoice.jpg" width="210" height="247" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bd/ConnieMitchellTheVoice.jpg/315px-ConnieMitchellTheVoice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bd/ConnieMitchellTheVoice.jpg/420px-ConnieMitchellTheVoice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="477" data-file-height="560" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ConnieMitchellTheVoice.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf6/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Connie_Mitchell" title="Connie Mitchell">Connie Mitchell</a> contributed vocals to several songs on the studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-linernotes_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linernotes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>, West revealed that he had worked with <a href="/wiki/Chris_Martin" title="Chris Martin">Chris Martin</a>, lead singer of the British <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative rock</a> band Coldplay, on a song entitled "<a href="/wiki/Homecoming_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Homecoming (Kanye West song)">Homecoming</a>," and that it might possibly be released as the <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a> for <i>Graduation</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-RollingWith_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RollingWith-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The collaboration occurred the year before when Kanye West and Chris Martin met one another during an impromptu jam session at <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road_Studios" title="Abbey Road Studios">Abbey Road Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NME_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NME-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> West had just finished performing at a show that had been held at Abbey Road and the band just so happened to be recording their music in the recording studio at exactly the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-Park_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Park-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> The song itself is a re-vamping for "Home," a track that was made available four years earlier on West's 2003 mixtape <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Get_Well_Soon...&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Get Well Soon... (page does not exist)">Get Well Soon...</a></i> and also later on the advance copy of <i><a href="/wiki/The_College_Dropout" title="The College Dropout">The College Dropout</a></i>, which due to a <a href="/wiki/Internet_leak" title="Internet leak">leak</a> was never released.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Globe_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> The original version possessed Kanye West's once trademark sped-up <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soulful</a> vocal sample production style, with singer <a href="/wiki/John_Legend" title="John Legend">John Legend</a> on the song's main chorus.<sup id="cite_ref-Globe_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Widely considered to be the most radio-friendly track on <i>Graduation</i>, West defines the album's third single "<a href="/wiki/Good_Life_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Good Life (Kanye West song)">Good Life</a>" as the song with the most "blatant <a href="/wiki/Hit_record" title="Hit record">hit-recordness</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> During his brief stay in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, he sent through sixteen different <a href="/wiki/Audio_mixing_(recorded_music)" title="Audio mixing (recorded music)">mixes</a> of the track over to their studio for the <a href="/wiki/Audio_mastering" title="Audio mastering">audio mastering</a> process.<sup id="cite_ref-Vozick-Levinson_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vozick-Levinson-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> West admitted that he actually did not really care for the single, but he was pressured into releasing it by his record label <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a>. However, West has clarified that he doesn't retain any lingering animosity towards his record label on this.<sup id="cite_ref-Kathwadia_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kathwadia-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>More than any other song on the entire studio album, the stadium-rap <a href="/wiki/Ballad#power_ballad" title="Ballad">power ballad</a> "I Wonder" was the most influenced by U2.<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Kanye went as far to cite it as one of this three most favorite songs from <i>Graduation</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Loop_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Loop-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> West imparted that he had sought out to make the hip-hop equivalent to the rock band's "<a href="/wiki/City_of_Blinding_Lights" title="City of Blinding Lights">City of Blinding Lights</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> He claimed that he heard the <a href="/wiki/Snare_drum" title="Snare drum">snare drum</a> that was used on the track while shopping for furniture at a <a href="/wiki/Moss_Bros_Group" title="Moss Bros Group">Moss</a> and spent many weeks working on it.<sup id="cite_ref-Caramanica_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caramanica-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bainbridge_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bainbridge-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> West has also said that he wrote the song while thinking of performing it onstage in front of an audience of over 50,000 people. With this in mind, he concentrated on speaking <a href="/wiki/Loudness" title="Loudness">volumes</a> with fewer wording and initially delivered all of his rapping in an intense <a href="/wiki/Staccato" title="Staccato">staccato</a> vocal style; <a href="/wiki/Elocution" title="Elocution">enunciating</a> and stressing each syllable in every word before transitioning to a faster, more fluid <a href="/wiki/Rapping#Flow" title="Rapping">flow</a> during the song's second verse.<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Powers_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Powers-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> West even considered releasing "I Wonder" as the album's fourth single but in the end, he instead chose "<a href="/wiki/Flashing_Lights_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Flashing Lights (Kanye West song)">Flashing Lights</a>," which he referred to as the "coolest" song on the album.<sup id="cite_ref-Loop_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Loop-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Graduation</i> started taking definite form around the time of the filming of the <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music video</a> for its second single "<a href="/wiki/Stronger_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Stronger (Kanye West song)">Stronger</a>," whereas prior West had been "aimlessly making songs."<sup id="cite_ref-Motorcycle_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Motorcycle-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">sci-fi</a> imagery of the <a href="/wiki/Hype_Williams" title="Hype Williams">Hype Williams</a>-directed video inspired West to take his music in a more futuristic direction.<sup id="cite_ref-Motorcycle_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Motorcycle-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> After the filming of the music video, which began before West had even written the song's second verse, he returned to the studio to redo parts of "Stronger" and various other tracks he recorded for the album, watching films like <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Recall_(1990_film)" title="Total Recall (1990 film)">Total Recall</a></i> for more ideas.<sup id="cite_ref-Motorcycle_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Motorcycle-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> West mixed the song seventy-five times, as he could not seem to get the <a href="/wiki/Bass_drum" title="Bass drum">bass drum</a> to sound precisely the way that he wanted it to.<sup id="cite_ref-Vozick-Levinson_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vozick-Levinson-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> He worked on "Stronger" with eight different <a href="/wiki/Audio_engineer" title="Audio engineer">audio engineers</a> around the world and recorded over fifty versions of the track.<sup id="cite_ref-Bainbridge_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bainbridge-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Still feeling dissatisfied after hearing the song in a club alongside <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a>'s 2007 single "<a href="/wiki/The_Way_I_Are" title="The Way I Are">The Way I Are</a>," West enlisted the hip-hop record producer to assist him in redoing its <a href="/wiki/Programming_(music)" title="Programming (music)">drum programming</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kathwadia_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kathwadia-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Graduation</i> also sees the return of composer and multi-instrumentalist <a href="/wiki/Jon_Brion" title="Jon Brion">Jon Brion</a>—who had played a key role as the co-execute producer on <i>Late Registration</i>—for "Drunk and Hot Girls."<sup id="cite_ref-RollingWith_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RollingWith-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DJ_Premier_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/DJ_Premier_2008.jpg/190px-DJ_Premier_2008.jpg" width="190" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/DJ_Premier_2008.jpg/285px-DJ_Premier_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/DJ_Premier_2008.jpg/380px-DJ_Premier_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1909" data-file-height="2332" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DJ_Premier_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf6/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The track "Everything I Am" features scratching by <a href="/wiki/DJ_Premier" title="DJ Premier">DJ Premier</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Beat_(music)" title="Beat (music)">beat</a> for "The Glory" was originally conceived for West's GOOD Music associate, close friend, and fellow <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> hip-hop artist <a href="/wiki/Common_(rapper)" title="Common (rapper)">Common</a>, whose seventh studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Forever" title="Finding Forever">Finding Forever</a></i> was being produced and recorded by West simultaneously with <i>Graduation</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ready_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ready-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> As was the case with their previous albums, certain tracks that West originally crafted for <i>Finding Forever</i> that Common declined eventually ended up on his own studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> "Everything I Am" was yet another song which was forged for Common that was passed on, a fact which West addresses within its opening lines.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The record features <a href="/wiki/Scratching" title="Scratching">scratching</a> contributed by famed hip-hop record producer DJ Premier.<sup id="cite_ref-Powers_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Powers-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> After West had played the <a href="/wiki/Demo_(music)" title="Demo (music)">demo</a> for "Everything I Am" over the phone for Premier and asked him what he thought of it, Premier replied that he enjoyed the lyrics and the innovative beat and offered to scratch over it.<sup id="cite_ref-Premier_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Premier-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> When working on the song, and while following numerous instructions that were supplied to him by West, DJ Premier took seven different styles of scratches, including <a href="/wiki/Drum_break" title="Drum break" class="mw-redirect">drum breaks</a>, cut them up into different <a href="/wiki/Rhythm" title="Rhythm">rhythms</a>, and scattered them all throughout the track, thus providing West with several different ideas for him to choose from.<sup id="cite_ref-Premier_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Premier-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>While written by West, who envisioned its concept and hook while riding an elevator, the Jay-Z dedication "<a href="/wiki/Big_Brother_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Big Brother (Kanye West song)">Big Brother</a>" stands as the only song on <i>Graduation</i> that he did not produce.<sup id="cite_ref-linernotes_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linernotes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The production of the track was instead handled solely by <a href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" title="Atlanta, Georgia" class="mw-redirect">Atlanta</a> record producer <a href="/wiki/DJ_Toomp" title="DJ Toomp">DJ Toomp</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-linernotes_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linernotes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> According to West's cousin, soul singer <a href="/wiki/The_World_Famous_Tony_Williams" title="The World Famous Tony Williams">Tony Williams</a>, Jay-Z became quite emotional after West played a part of "Big Brother" for him in the studio for the very first time.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, West himself recalled that it was "a very serious moment."<sup id="cite_ref-Praise_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Praise-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> When asked for his opinion, Jay-Z replied that he considered "Big Brother" a fair portrayal from a little brother's perspective. He also said that he thought the song was "brilliantly written" and Kanye's best song since "<a href="/wiki/Jesus_Walks_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Jesus Walks (Kanye West song)" class="mw-redirect">Jesus Walks</a>" as far as structure and emotion.<sup id="cite_ref-Vozick-Levinson_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vozick-Levinson-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Although "Bittersweet Poetry" appears as an <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Bonus_track" title="Bonus track">bonus track</a> on <i>Graduation</i>, it was actually one of the very first songs crafted for <i>Late Registration</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Diamonds_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diamonds-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> After seeing the 2004 biographical film <i><a href="/wiki/Ray_(film)" title="Ray (film)">Ray</a></i> together, Kanye West and <a href="/wiki/Blues_rock" title="Blues rock">blues-rock</a> musician <a href="/wiki/John_Mayer" title="John Mayer">John Mayer</a> decided to collaborate on a record and immediately went back to the recording studio to compose the song "Bittersweet."<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> This wasn't the first time West and Mayer collaborated with one another. The two previously worked together to make "<a href="/wiki/Go!_(Common_song)" title="Go! (Common song)">Go!</a>," the third single from Common's sixth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Be_(Common_album)" title="Be (Common album)">Be</a></i>, which came about when Mayer went to visit West at The Record Plant in Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-Elaborate_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elaborate-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> In the end, because West felt that their song did not coincide well into the overall soundscape of his second album, it was subsequently not included.<sup id="cite_ref-Globe_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_style">Music and style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Music and style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With <i>Graduation</i>, West departed from the warm <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> samples of <i>The College Dropout</i> and the lush <a href="/wiki/Baroque_pop" title="Baroque pop">baroque-pop</a> orchestration of <i>Late Registration</i> and moved towards a more atmospheric, <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a>-tinged, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic</a>-influenced soundscape.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The musical evolution arose from him listening to music genres encompassing European <a href="/wiki/Britpop" title="Britpop">Britpop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Euro_disco" title="Euro disco">Euro-disco</a>, American <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indie_rock" title="Indie rock">indie-rock</a>, and his native <a href="/wiki/Chicago_house" title="Chicago house">Chicago house</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Park_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Park-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pytlik_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pytlik-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Towards this end, West retracted much of the <a href="/wiki/Live_instrumentation" title="Live instrumentation">live instrumentation</a> that characterized his previous album and had it replaced with heavy, <a href="/wiki/Gothic_rock" title="Gothic rock">gothic</a> <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synths</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lynskey_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lynskey-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> West injected <a href="/wiki/Distortion_(music)" title="Distortion (music)">distorted</a> synth-chords, <a href="/wiki/Rave_music" title="Rave music">rave</a> stabs, <a href="/wiki/House_music" title="House music">house</a> beats, <a href="/wiki/Electro_music" title="Electro music" class="mw-redirect">electro</a>-<a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a> rhythms, and a wide array of <a href="/wiki/Modulation_(music)" title="Modulation (music)">modulated</a> electronic <a href="/wiki/Noise_music" title="Noise music">noises</a> and digital <a href="/wiki/Audio_signal_processing" title="Audio signal processing">sound-effects</a> into his <a href="/wiki/Articulation_(music)" title="Articulation (music)">articulate</a> hip-hop production.<sup id="cite_ref-Pytlik_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pytlik-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brett_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brett-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the dominant synthetic attributes, the emphasis on organic <a href="/wiki/String_arrangement" title="String arrangement" class="mw-redirect">string arrangements</a> that had accentuated <i>Late Registration</i> remained a significant factor on <i>Graduation</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Serwer_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Serwer-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Praise_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Praise-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Also, similar to its predecessor, the album didn't relegate itself to the conventional <a href="/wiki/Loop_(music)" title="Loop (music)">looping</a> techniques typical of contemporary hip-hop and instead continued to implement sudden musical <a href="/wiki/Shift_(music)" title="Shift (music)" class="mw-redirect">shifts</a> within its multi-layered song structures and express intricately composed <a href="/wiki/Introduction_(music)" title="Introduction (music)">introductions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bridge_(music)" title="Bridge (music)">bridges</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coda_(music)" title="Coda (music)">codas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vibe_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vibe-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Under the belief that his previous album had been too indulgent and poorly arranged, West fashioned <i>Graduation</i> to contain less ornate production, made the album completely devoid of <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_skit" title="Hip hop skit">skits</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Music_sequencer" title="Music sequencer">sequenced</a> it in such a way that it produced a tighter, more cohesive package.<sup id="cite_ref-Praise_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Praise-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brackett_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brackett-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="mbox-small" style="border:1px solid #aaa; background-color:#f9f9f9;">

<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">

</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em;">
