<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em;"><span style="font-size:smaller;"><i>Problems playing these files? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>Graduation</i> opens on a sparse note with "<a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Good Morning (Kanye West song)">Good Morning</a>," beginning with an echoed, metronomic <a href="/wiki/Cowbell_(instrument)" title="Cowbell (instrument)">cowbell</a> beat and a thumping <a href="/wiki/Bassline" title="Bassline">bassline</a> melded with a simple, <a href="/wiki/Arpeggio" title="Arpeggio">arpeggiating</a> synthesizer <a href="/wiki/Drone_(music)" title="Drone (music)">drone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-D._52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D.-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The drone is drowned by the music that arrives at the chorus, which is a conflation of <a href="/wiki/Ambient_music" title="Ambient music">ambient</a> synths and an astral backing <a href="/wiki/Choir" title="Choir">choir</a> crafted from a non-verbal vocal sample of "<a href="/wiki/Someone_Saved_My_Life_Tonight" title="Someone Saved My Life Tonight">Someone Saved My Life Tonight</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bainbridge_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bainbridge-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> "Good Morning" concludes with the voice of Jay-Z reiterating lyrics from "The Ruler's Back," the rapper's own opening track of his sixth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Blueprint" title="The Blueprint">The Blueprint</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brackett_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brackett-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The production for "<a href="/wiki/Champion_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Champion (Kanye West song)">Champion</a>" features intermittent <a href="/wiki/Drop_(music)" title="Drop (music)">drops</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roland_TR-808" title="Roland TR-808">808</a>-<a href="/wiki/Clapping#Musical_works_that_include_clapping" title="Clapping">handclaps</a> and expresses a slight <a href="/wiki/Jazz_fusion" title="Jazz fusion">jazz-rock</a> influence, eschewing guitars and trumpets in favor of breezy synths.<sup id="cite_ref-D._52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D.-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Song_structure_(popular_music)#Verse" title="Song structure (popular music)">verses</a>, West raps over a constant loop of the words "their eyes" while the chopped-up <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hook</a> is formed from the question, "Did you realize, that you were a champion?"<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Both phrases are recontextualized from a line lifted from "<a href="/wiki/Kid_Charlemagne" title="Kid Charlemagne">Kid Charlemagne</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Steely_Dan" title="Steely Dan">Steely Dan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> The song also sports a <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a>-inspired bridge delivered by <a href="/wiki/Connie_Mitchell" title="Connie Mitchell">Connie Mitchell</a> in a distinct <a href="/wiki/Deejay_(Jamaican)#Toasting" title="Deejay (Jamaican)">toasting</a> vocal style.<sup id="cite_ref-Favorite_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Favorite-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> More than any other song on the entire album, "I Wonder" was the most influenced by U2, as West imparted that he sought to make the hip-hop equivalent to the band's "<a href="/wiki/City_of_Blinding_Lights" title="City of Blinding Lights">City of Blinding Lights</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Described by music critics as "stadium-rap," the soul-fired track starts off with its piano-based <a href="/wiki/Refrain" title="Refrain">refrain</a>, which contains samples of "My Song" by British poet <a href="/wiki/Labi_Siffre" title="Labi Siffre">Labi Siffre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> It then proceeds to morph into a myriad of interlaced synths that are impacted by <a href="/wiki/Distortion_(music)" title="Distortion (music)">distorted</a> snare drum strokes and ethereal <a href="/wiki/Electronic_keyboard" title="Electronic keyboard">electronic keyboards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pytlik_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pytlik-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> During the bridge, the <a href="/wiki/Chord_progression" title="Chord progression">chord progression</a> changes and the song adopts a heavy <a href="/wiki/String_section" title="String section">string section</a> that emulates the <a href="/wiki/Melody" title="Melody">melody</a> of its synths. The composition then enters an instrumental passage and finishes off with a sweeping string arrangement.<sup id="cite_ref-Pytlik_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pytlik-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"Good Life" utilizes multi-tracked, interlocking vocals that harmonize with guest singer T-Pain's <a href="/wiki/Auto-Tune" title="Auto-Tune">Auto-Tuned</a> voice. The song's <a href="/wiki/Melody" title="Melody">melody</a> is based on sampled keyboards from <a href="/wiki/Pretty_Young_Thing" title="Pretty Young Thing" class="mw-redirect">P.Y.T.</a> by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">tempo</a> slightly decreased and the <a href="/wiki/Pitch_(music)" title="Pitch (music)">pitch</a> raised to the point its sound resembles squealing shrieks.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> "Barry Bonds" is built on a moaning bass line and Gothic organ, while punctuated by wailing sampled from "Long Red" by <a href="/wiki/Mountain_(band)" title="Mountain (band)">Mountain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brackett_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brackett-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Heaton_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heaton-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> "Drunk and Hot Girls" exhibits a sluggish <a href="/wiki/Waltz" title="Waltz">waltz</a> pitched with the <a href="/wiki/Rhythm" title="Rhythm">rhythm</a> of an <a href="/wiki/Eastern_European" title="Eastern European" class="mw-redirect">Eastern European</a> <a href="/wiki/Drinking_song" title="Drinking song">drinking song</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NME_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NME-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> It contains a mix of <a href="/wiki/Dark_music" title="Dark music" class="mw-redirect">dark</a> orchestration and detuned electronics with elements of "Sing Swan Song" by <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">German</a> <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Can_(band)" title="Can (band)">Can</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pytlik_46-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pytlik-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> West claimed that while listening to their song, he heard the words "drunk and hot girls" rather than the actual "drunky hot bowls" lyrics.<sup id="cite_ref-Scaggs_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scaggs-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Rather than rap, West and guest artist Mos Def sing along to the song's melody.<sup id="cite_ref-Heaton_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heaton-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Opening with a gradual, rising crescendo of symphonic <a href="/wiki/Strings_(music)" title="Strings (music)" class="mw-redirect">strings</a>, "Flashing Lights" emits synth twinklings before transforming into a moderately-paced, synth-driven beat. After the <a href="/wiki/Introduction_(music)" title="Introduction (music)">introduction</a>, in which Mitchell's processed vocals repeat the titular <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hook</a> four times, West raps the two verses, each one followed by the <a href="/wiki/Refrain" title="Refrain">chorus</a> sung by Dwele coupled with the hook. Following a <a href="/wiki/Break_(music)" title="Break (music)">break</a>, the song enters a passage where its heavily manipulated hook echoes in and out before the <a href="/wiki/Coda_(music)" title="Coda (music)">coda</a> draws the composition to a close.<sup id="cite_ref-linernotes_18-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linernotes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> "Stronger" is built around a sample of "<a href="/wiki/Harder,_Better,_Faster,_Stronger" title="Harder, Better, Faster, Stronger">Harder, Better, Faster, Stronger</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Daft_Punk" title="Daft Punk">Daft Punk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-linernotes_18-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linernotes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>By being composed using nothing more than a <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_piano" title="Rhodes piano">Rhodes piano</a>, a vocal sample, and some <a href="/wiki/Scratching" title="Scratching">scratching</a>, "Everything I Am" stands as the third studio album's most <a href="/wiki/Minimal_music" title="Minimal music">minimalistic</a> production.<sup id="cite_ref-Rizov_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rizov-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> West marries a <a href="/wiki/Downtempo" title="Downtempo">down-tempo</a> beat to gentle piano chords that are accentuated by soulful cooing sampled from "If We Can't Be Lovers" by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Phillip_Mitchell" title="Prince Phillip Mitchell" class="mw-redirect">Prince Phillip Mitchell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-linernotes_18-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linernotes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The song features a scratched hook by <a href="/wiki/DJ_Premier" title="DJ Premier">DJ Premier</a> formed with the vocal sample, which contains the line, "Here we go again," which is lifted from "<a href="/wiki/Bring_the_Noise" title="Bring the Noise">Bring the Noise</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Public_Enemy_(group)" title="Public Enemy (group)">Public Enemy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> With its high-speed <a href="/wiki/Bass_drum" title="Bass drum">bass drum</a> pattern, "The Glory" is an up-tempo number which revisits the "<a href="/wiki/Alvin_and_the_Chipmunks#Recording_technique" title="Alvin and the Chipmunks">chipmunk</a>-<a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a>" that defined West's early production style.<sup id="cite_ref-Serwer_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Serwer-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> It displays a sped-up, <a href="/wiki/Pitch_(music)" title="Pitch (music)">high-pitch</a> vocal sample of "Save The Country" by <a href="/wiki/Laura_Nyro" title="Laura Nyro">Laura Nyro</a> accompanied by uplifting string and a <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel choir</a> symphony.<sup id="cite_ref-Kellman_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kellman-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a> lead vocalist <a href="/wiki/Chris_Martin" title="Chris Martin">Chris Martin</a> sings the chorus and supplies a gospel-flavored piano <a href="/wiki/Motif_(music)" title="Motif (music)">motif</a> while West raps over heavy yet buoyant drums on "<a href="/wiki/Homecoming_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Homecoming (Kanye West song)">Homecoming</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-Globe_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Scaggs_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scaggs-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The chatter of a noisy, cheering crowd can inexplicably be heard in the background throughout the song.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> The Jay-Z ode "<a href="/wiki/Big_Brother_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Big Brother (Kanye West song)">Big Brother</a>" begins with West uttering the words, "Stadium status ...," backed by a string section, pounding drums, a distorted <a href="/wiki/Ostinato#Riff" title="Ostinato">guitar riff</a> and plinking piano keys.<sup id="cite_ref-linernotes_18-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linernotes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Around mid-verse, the track adopts synths that replicate the melody of the live strings. Before its second verse, the song is adorned with more musical devices, including a <a href="/wiki/Bassline" title="Bassline">bass-line</a>, metallic <a href="/wiki/Percussion_instrument" title="Percussion instrument">percussion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Roland_TR-808" title="Roland TR-808">808</a>-<a href="/wiki/Clapping#Musical_works_that_include_clapping" title="Clapping">handclaps</a>. The final track "Good Night" exhibits the production characteristics of West's next musical evolution. West juxtaposes the <a href="/wiki/Glitch_(music)" title="Glitch (music)">glitchy</a>, mechanical sound of an <a href="/wiki/8-bit_(music)" title="8-bit (music)" class="mw-redirect">8-Bit</a> beat with the elegant, traditional sound of the classical piano.<sup id="cite_ref-NME_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NME-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lyrical_content">Lyrical content</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Lyrical content">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:K._West_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/K._West_%28cropped%29.jpg/180px-K._West_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="180" height="287" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/K._West_%28cropped%29.jpg/270px-K._West_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c8/K._West_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="290" data-file-height="462" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:K._West_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf6/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
West wrote lyrics expressing an ambivalence towards his newfound wealth and fame.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In comparison to previous albums, which were largely driven by observational commentary on matters pertaining to social welfare, <i>Graduation</i> is more introspective in nature and addresses personal themes.<sup id="cite_ref-Drumming_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Drumming-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Henderson_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Henderson-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> West stated that he wanted to make inspirational music and placed more focus on individual perspective and experience that listeners could connect with in an attempt to create "people's theme songs."<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Dismayed that the messages behind his complex lyricism were frequently lost on listeners and didn't carry well during live performances, West made an attempt to simplify his lyrics and use more skeletal <a href="/wiki/Rhyme_scheme" title="Rhyme scheme">rhyme schemes</a> for more straightforward verses while concentrating on speaking volumes with sparser wording on <i>Graduation</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Having committed a significant amount of time towards elevating his story-telling ability by listening to <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk</a> musicians, West manages to form a lyrical narrative within nearly every song on the album.<sup id="cite_ref-Praise_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Praise-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> West dedicated a majority of the album towards conducting an analysis himself and conveying his ambivalent outlook on his newfound wealth and fame. As such, West's subversive songwriting fluctuates between playful self-aggrandizement and critical self-doubt.<sup id="cite_ref-Cowie_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cowie-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> While confident, extroverted and celebratory at face value, many songs contained on <i>Graduation</i> were thematically distanced and retained <a href="/wiki/Melancholic" title="Melancholic" class="mw-redirect">melancholic</a> subtext.<sup id="cite_ref-Kellman_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kellman-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Some music critics remarked that compounded with West's urgent, emotive <a href="/wiki/Rapping" title="Rapping">rapping</a> style, the record sounded as if he were experiencing an <a href="/wiki/Existentialism" title="Existentialism">existential</a> crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-PopCD_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopCD-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Free_association_(psychology)" title="Free association (psychology)">free-associative</a> "Champion" is primarily composed of motivational lyrics, but West also briefly touches on the strained relationship he had with his father–who divorced from his mother when he was just three-years-old–eventually reaching the conclusion that even with their ups and downs, in the end, his father was a champion in his eyes.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> West described "Stronger" as an "emancipation", as he uses the song to vent his frustration over mistakes he has made in the past.<sup id="cite_ref-Motorcycle_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Motorcycle-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> "I Wonder" carries an introspective tone, retaining a chorus about finding one's dreams, while West uses the verses to describe the struggle a person experiences in determining the meaning behind their life and achieving those dreams.<sup id="cite_ref-Heaton_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heaton-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Inspired by watching Bono open stadium tours, West concentrated on speaking volumes without using too many words on the song and delivers his raps in an exuberant, <a href="/wiki/Staccato" title="Staccato">staccato</a> manner.<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Using the same vocal stylings, "Flashing Lights" tells the operatic narrative of man contemplating the complexities of a tragic relationship. "Can't Tell Me Nothing" serves as West's reflection on his fame and is characterized by bitter remorse and defiant self-awareness. West begins the song by expounding his conflicted feelings regarding wealth and desire, describing a compulsion to spend that overwhelms any and all other objectives in life.<sup id="cite_ref-Heaton_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heaton-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> He ties this into his perceived overall inability to keep himself together even as he grows into an increasingly prominent figure in the public eye.<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>West regains his lyrical dexterity on "Barry Bonds", a competitive, though friendly battle with Lil Wayne in which the two MCs exchange <a href="/wiki/Braggadocio_(rap)" title="Braggadocio (rap)">braggadocios</a> rhymes.<sup id="cite_ref-BarryBonds_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BarryBonds-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The song uses <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> player <a href="/wiki/Barry_Bonds" title="Barry Bonds">Barry Bonds</a> as a metaphor for West's ability to create music hits.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> "Drunk and Hot Girls" is a first-person narrative that illustrates a man courting an intoxicated woman in a club but gets more than what he bargained for.<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> "Everything I Am" is a song of self-examination, in which West attempts to confront his fallacies by surveying the consequences of his outspokeness ruminating over various ways people expect him to conduct himself. In the track, West addresses his indifference towards constructing a <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangster</a> persona, his refusal to dress and act like every other rapper, his inclination towards social commentary, and his lack of self-restraint.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> West comes to the conclusion that while he will never be able to live up to people's expectations and will always be disadvantageously flawed; it's all these imperfections and more that serve to make up who he is.<sup id="cite_ref-Heaton_56-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heaton-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> When writing the song, West thought of a young girl in <a href="/wiki/High_school" title="High school">high school</a> dealing with people coming down on her.<sup id="cite_ref-Praise_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Praise-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"Homecoming" serves as a heartfelt tribute to West's hometown of <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>. Using an <a href="/wiki/Extended_metaphor" title="Extended metaphor">extended metaphor</a> that personifies the city as a <a href="/wiki/Childhood_sweetheart" title="Childhood sweetheart">childhood sweetheart</a> named Wendy, West rhymes about his love for Chicago and his guilt over leaving "her" to pursue stardom.<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The song's opening lines lyrically paraphrase "<a href="/wiki/I_Used_to_Love_H.E.R." title="I Used to Love H.E.R.">I Used to Love H.E.R.</a>," a similarly metaphoric hip-hop song made by West's close friend and labelmate <a href="/wiki/Common_(rapper)" title="Common (rapper)">Common</a>, who later appeared in the single's music video.<sup id="cite_ref-NME_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NME-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> West dedicated "<a href="/wiki/Big_Brother_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Big Brother (Kanye West song)">Big Brother</a>" to <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, whom he feels so close to that he sees him as a brother. Within the song, West dually details his love and admiration as well as his envy and antagonism towards Jay-Z, metaphorically equating their relationship to that of a <a href="/wiki/Sibling_rivalry" title="Sibling rivalry">sibling rivalry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Praise_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Praise-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> West also uses the song's chorus as a subsidiary dedication to his mentor <a href="/wiki/No_I.D." title="No I.D.">No I.D.</a>, who first taught him how to produce music.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> Similar to its musicality, the songwriting characteristics of the album-closing track, "Good Night" alludes to West's next musical evolution. The majority of song is composed of repetitive recitations of its choruses and bridges by Mos Def and <a href="/wiki/Albert_Daniels" title="Albert Daniels">Al Be Back</a>. West melodically raps only one single verse in which he nostalgically reminisces over taking trips to the museum with his grandparents. As his verse draws to a close, West chastises that a person can't dwell on the past, and charges himself with living his life like he has no tomorrow. In retrospect, with the death of his mother Donda West less than two months after the album was released in addition to the dissolution of his engagement with fiancée Alexis Phifer, the trace amounts of melancholy found scattered throughout <i>Graduation</i> would all but envelop West's next studio album, <i>808s &amp; Heartbreak</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artwork">Artwork</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Artwork">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dropout_Bear_Grad.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ac/Dropout_Bear_Grad.png/250px-Dropout_Bear_Grad.png" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/ac/Dropout_Bear_Grad.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/ac/Dropout_Bear_Grad.png 2x" data-file-width="352" data-file-height="264" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dropout_Bear_Grad.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf6/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
Dropout Bear being pursued by a monstrous cloud within the interior artwork of <i>Graduation</i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>West collaborated with Japanese contemporary artist <a href="/wiki/Takashi_Murakami" title="Takashi Murakami">Takashi Murakami</a> to oversee the art direction of <i>Graduation</i> as well as design the cover art for the album's accompanying singles.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Often called "the <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol">Warhol</a> of Japan," Murakami's surrealistic visual art is characterized by cartoonish creatures that appear friendly and cheerful at first glance, but possess dark, twisted undertones.<sup id="cite_ref-warhol_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warhol-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The collaboration between the two came about when West visited Murakami's <a href="/wiki/Kaikai_Kiki" title="Kaikai Kiki">Kaikai Kiki</a> studio in <a href="/wiki/Roppongi_Hills" title="Roppongi Hills">Roppongi Hills</a> during a brief trip to <a href="/wiki/Tokyo,_Japan" title="Tokyo, Japan" class="mw-redirect">Tokyo, Japan</a> in the midst of touring the year before.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The album's <a href="/wiki/Album_artwork" title="Album artwork" class="mw-redirect">artwork</a> expresses colorful, pastel imagery influenced by Murakami's affiliation with <a href="/wiki/Superflat" title="Superflat">superflat</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Postmodern_art" title="Postmodern art">post-modern art</a> movement influenced by <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">manga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Its production process took place over the course of several weeks, with West constantly visualizing new images and emailing the ideas to Murakami and his team.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Bringing the educational theme expressed by West's previous albums to a close, the visual plotline of the images contained within the <a href="/wiki/Liner_notes" title="Liner notes">liner notes</a> lead up to a graduation ceremony that takes places within a fictional college institution situated within a futuristic metropolis called Universe City.<sup id="cite_ref-Ready_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ready-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> Murakami explained the metaphor behind the artwork saying:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The cover is based on Kanye's theme of student life. School. It's a place of dreams, of righteousness, a place to have fun. It's also occasionally a place where you experience the rigid <a href="/wiki/Dogma" title="Dogma">dogma</a> of the human race. Kanye's music scrapes sentimentality and aggressiveness together like <a href="/wiki/Sandpaper" title="Sandpaper">sandpaper</a>, and he uses his <a href="/wiki/Groove_(music)" title="Groove (music)">grooves</a> to unleash this tornado that spins with the zeitgeist of the times. I too wanted to be swept up and spun around in that tornado.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="templatequotecite">—Takashi Murakami</div>
</blockquote>
<p>The artwork's storyline centers around "Dropout Bear," West's <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphic" title="Anthropomorphic" class="mw-redirect">anthropomorphic</a> teddy bear mascot.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> The illustrations chronicle Dropout Bear overcoming various obstacles in an effort to reach his college campus in time for his graduation ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-itunes_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itunes-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> The story begins on a rainy day with Dropout being awoken by his <a href="/wiki/Alarm_clock" title="Alarm clock">alarm clock</a> and running out of his apartment to his car, modeled after a <a href="/wiki/DeLorean_time_machine" title="DeLorean time machine">DeLorean</a>. When the car's engine dies, he is forced to find an alternative means of transportation.<sup id="cite_ref-warhol_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warhol-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Dropout attempts to hail a cab but it speeds right past him, soaking him with puddle water. He then tries to get onto a <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro rail</a> but just misses it as it pulls away. Left with no other options, Dropout is reduced to pursuing his goal on foot. As he races down sidewalks, populated by multi-eyed, living mushrooms, Dropout is pursued by a monstrous rain cloud that attempts to swallow him whole.<sup id="cite_ref-goodmorning_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-goodmorning-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> Eventually, Dropout Bear arrives at the university and makes it to his ceremony just in time to stand before his colleagues, a wide variety of anthropomorphic creatures like himself. The visual story concludes with Dropout Bear being catapulted from the university into the sky on the back cover.<sup id="cite_ref-linernotes_18-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linernotes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The cover art for <i>Graduation</i> was cited as the fifth best album cover of the year by <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> The designs of the album artwork were later brought to life by Murakami through the use of <a href="/wiki/Cel-shaded_animation" title="Cel-shaded animation" class="mw-redirect">cel-shaded animation</a> within a three-minute animated <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music video</a> for "Good Morning."<sup id="cite_ref-goodmorning_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-goodmorning-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:50_cent_in_concert.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/50_cent_in_concert.jpg/250px-50_cent_in_concert.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/50_cent_in_concert.jpg/375px-50_cent_in_concert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/50_cent_in_concert.jpg/500px-50_cent_in_concert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:50_cent_in_concert.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf6/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
Publicity over the album's release date pitted West in a sales competition against rapper 50 Cent (pictured).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While hosting a listening session for his second studio album <i>Late Registration</i> on August 3, 2005 at <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Studios" title="Sony Music Studios">Sony Music Studios</a>, West revealed that he wished to schedule the release of his third album <i>Graduation</i> sometime around October 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Several months later, on March 28, 2007, West appeared on the Los Angeles radio station <a href="/wiki/KPWR" title="KPWR">Power 106</a>. He said that he was working on his third album as well as Common's seventh album <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Forever" title="Finding Forever">Finding Forever</a></i> and rapped a few lyrics from one of his songs in <a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> On May 11, it was announced that the release date for <i>Graduation</i> was September 18, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Ready_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ready-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> West debuted the album's lead single "Can't Tell Me Nothing" on the New York radio station <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">Hot 97</a> on May 15.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> He then released a free <a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Tell_Me_Nothing_(mixtape)" title="Can't Tell Me Nothing (mixtape)">mixtape under the same name</a> onto the Internet on May 27.<sup id="cite_ref-Apocalypto_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Apocalypto-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> The mixtape featured preview clips of songs that would later appear on <i>Graduation</i> and showcased various artists signed onto West's <a href="/wiki/GOOD_Music" title="GOOD Music">GOOD Music</a> record label as well as collaborations with other unaffiliated musicians.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> It also contained "<a href="/wiki/Us_Placers" title="Us Placers">Us Placers</a>", the debut song of <a href="/wiki/Child_Rebel_Soldier" title="Child Rebel Soldier">Child Rebel Soldier</a>, a supergroup West had formed with <a href="/wiki/Lupe_Fiasco" title="Lupe Fiasco">Lupe Fiasco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Apocalypto_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Apocalypto-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>At the end of May, <a href="/wiki/Island_Def_Jam" title="Island Def Jam" class="mw-redirect">Island Def Jam</a> pushed forward the release date for <i>Graduation</i> up from September to an unspecified late August date, a decision that West first announced on the introductory track of his <i>Can't Tell Me Nothing</i> mixtape.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> On July 19, the album's release date was changed once more and moved to September 11, 2007, the same US release date as rapper <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a>'s third studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Curtis_(50_Cent_album)" title="Curtis (50 Cent album)">Curtis</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> When first presented with the proposal of his label moving the release date of his album yet again as well as the idea of a sales race between him and 50 Cent, West initially expressed his indifference towards the thought, saying, "When I heard that thing about the debate, I thought that was the stupidest thing. When my album drops and 50's album drops, everybody wins because you're gonna get a lot of good music at the same time."<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> However, then Def Jam president and CEO <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> welcomed competition, feeling that it would be prosperous for hip-hop and the date became permanent.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The album's release generated much publicity over a sales competition with 50 Cent's <i>Curtis</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rodriguez_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Three months that were prior to the September 11 release date, West extended his gratitude towards 50 Cent for the enthusiasm and excitement the friendly competition had produced. Though confident that he would emerge victorious, West said that he would be perfectly fine with losing to 50 Cent, saying that he'd rather, "be #2 on that day rather than come out and be #1 on a day nobody cares about."<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> In an interview for <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>, 50 Cent expressed his view on the idea of a sales competition, stating "It's great marketing — for Kanye West. But I sell way more records than Kanye West, and I generate way more interest than Kanye West. They think they can match us up, but they'll find out when that week goes by and the sales come back. This is no rivalry."<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> On August 10, 50 Cent stated during an interview with <a href="/wiki/SOHH" title="SOHH">SOHH</a> that he would end his career as a solo artist if <i>Graduation</i> sold more copies than <i>Curtis</i> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> However, he retracted his statement within an <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> interview due to contract agreements with <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion">Promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kanye_at_V_Festival_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Kanye_at_V_Festival_2007.jpg/250px-Kanye_at_V_Festival_2007.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Kanye_at_V_Festival_2007.jpg/375px-Kanye_at_V_Festival_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Kanye_at_V_Festival_2007.jpg/500px-Kanye_at_V_Festival_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kanye_at_V_Festival_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf6/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
West performing before a crowd at <a href="/wiki/V_Festival" title="V Festival">V Festival</a> on August 18, 2007 in Chelmsford, England.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>West spent a significant amount of time promoting <i>Graduation</i> during his trip to the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Push_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Push-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> On August 17, West guest starred on the British comedy-variety show <i><a href="/wiki/The_Friday_Night_Project" title="The Friday Night Project" class="mw-redirect">The Friday Night Project</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Push_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Push-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> He played preview versions of the songs "Big Brother" and "Champion" from his forthcoming third album while making an appearance on DJ <a href="/wiki/Tim_Westwood" title="Tim Westwood">Tim Westwood</a>'s radio show on August 18.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> Later that day, West performed at <a href="/wiki/V_Festival" title="V Festival">V Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chelmsford" title="Chelmsford">Chelmsford, England</a> before an audience of over 50,000 people and again played new material from <i>Graduation</i> as well as a tribute <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">cover</a> of <a href="/wiki/Amy_Winehouse" title="Amy Winehouse">Amy Winehouse</a>'s hit single "<a href="/wiki/Rehab_(Amy_Winehouse_song)" title="Rehab (Amy Winehouse song)">Rehab</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> He then held a secret concert with <a href="/wiki/Barbadian_people" title="Barbadian people">Barbadian</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a> for an audience of over five hundred fans and invited guests at <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Central_Hall" title="Westminster Central Hall" class="mw-redirect">Westminster Central Hall</a> in London, England on August 20.<sup id="cite_ref-Push_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Push-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ShoutOut_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShoutOut-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> The guests were greeted by staff members wearing graduation robes and <a href="/wiki/Mortarboard_cap" title="Mortarboard cap" class="mw-redirect">mortarboard caps</a> in reference to the title of West's third studio album <i>Graduation</i>. At the end of the show, silver confetti and ticker tape reading <i>Touch the Sky</i> fell from the ceiling onto the audience while the actual "<a href="/wiki/Touch_the_Sky" title="Touch the Sky">Touch the Sky</a>," which was the fourth single from <i>Late Registration</i>, was played on the speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-ShoutOut_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShoutOut-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After he returned to the United States, West joined 50 Cent onstage for a surprise performance before an audience of over 20,000 people at a show held on August 22 in <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> during <a href="/wiki/Ciara" title="Ciara">Ciara</a> and <a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Screamfest_%2707" title="Screamfest '07">Screamfest '07</a> tour.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> West performed for a benefit concert sponsored by his charity foundation on August 24 at Chicago's <a href="/wiki/House_of_Blues" title="House of Blues">House of Blues</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cohen_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> At the concert, he provided live renditions of songs from <i>Graduation</i> and gave the audience a sneak peek of the early production of his <a href="/wiki/Glow_in_the_Dark_Tour" title="Glow in the Dark Tour">Glow in the Dark Tour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cohen_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> On August 28, West hosted an album listening session for <i>Graduation</i> at <a href="/wiki/New_World_Stages" title="New World Stages">New World Stages</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> It was there that he explained his influences and aspirations for the album and played songs over <a href="/wiki/Video_clip" title="Video clip">video clips</a> taken from a variety of futuristic <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction_film" title="Science fiction film">sci-fi films</a>, including <i><a href="/wiki/Tron" title="Tron">Tron</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Akira_(film)" title="Akira (film)">Akira</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/2046_(film)" title="2046 (film)">2046</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/2001:_A_Space_Odyssey_(film)" title="2001: A Space Odyssey (film)">2001: A Space Odyssey</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-GradListen_2-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradListen-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Two days later, on the morning of August 30, a clean version of the album <a href="/wiki/Internet_leak" title="Internet leak">leaked</a> onto the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> In a survey conducted by <i>Billboard</i>, results displayed that an estimated 44% of readers predicted that <i>Graduation</i> would sell more units over 50 Cent and Kenny Chesney.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> Projections for first week scans based on early store sales reports indicated towards the 575,000–700,000 range for <i>Graduation</i>, while <i>Curtis</i> was projected in the 500,000–600,000 range.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width: 24%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 90%; background-color: #FFFFF0;">
<div style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div style="margin:0px 2em;">
<p>It's a great promotional tool. To me, it's the greatest thing ever. I think people should do it more often. I'm a fan of both albums. Hip-hop needs this right now.</p>
</div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">“</div>
<div style="position: absolute; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">”</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: right;"><a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a>, on the coinciding release of West's <i>Graduation</i> and <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Curtis_(50_Cent_album)" title="Curtis (50 Cent album)">Curtis</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>On the first day of its release, <i>Graduation</i> sold over 437,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-firstday_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firstday-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> The album debuted at number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, grossing a total of over 957,000 copies in its first week in the United States alone.<sup id="cite_ref-firstday_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firstday-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Graduation</i> became West's second consecutive studio album to top the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and also debuted at number-one on the album charts in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-canada_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canada-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> It was within the very same week that "Stronger" topped the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_100" title="Hot 100" class="mw-redirect">Hot 100</a>, selling over 205,000 <a href="/wiki/Music_download" title="Music download">digital downloads</a> and giving West his third number-one single.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon its release, <i>Graduation</i> achieved the highest first week sales week for any album in 2007, topping <a href="/wiki/Linkin_Park" title="Linkin Park">Linkin Park</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Minutes_to_Midnight_(album)" title="Minutes to Midnight (album)">Minutes to Midnight</a></i>, which sold 625,000 copies. The album was also West's highest first sales week to date, surpassing the 860,000 opening week of his previous album <i>Late Registration</i>. It registered the best first-week sales totals of any record released within the last two years, with the last being West's own <i>Late Registration</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Additionally, <i>Graduation</i> became ranked as the 15th highest sales week for an album since <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> began tracking data in 1991, as well as the highest sales week at the time of its release for an album since 50 Cent's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Massacre" title="The Massacre">The Massacre</a></i> (2005).<sup id="cite_ref-billboard_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> It also set the record for the largest week of an album digitally downloaded, registering over 133,000 paid downloads, beating <a href="/wiki/Maroon_5" title="Maroon 5">Maroon 5</a>'s previous set record of 102,000 for <i><a href="/wiki/It_Won%27t_Be_Soon_Before_Long" title="It Won't Be Soon Before Long">It Won't Be Soon Before Long</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Graduation</i>'s first week sales of 957,000 and <i>Curtis</i>'s first week sales of 691,000 marked only the second time ever since the inception of Nielsen SoundScan that two albums debuted within the same week with totals surpassing 600,000 copies in the United States. The first occurrence of such an event was in September 1991, when <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N' Roses">Guns N' Roses</a> conjunctively released <i><a href="/wiki/Use_Your_Illusion_I" title="Use Your Illusion I">Use Your Illusion I</a></i>, which sold 685,000 copies, and <i><a href="/wiki/Use_Your_Illusion_II" title="Use Your Illusion II">Use Your Illusion II</a></i>, which sold 770,000 copies. The first week sales totals of <i>Graduation</i> and <i>Curtis</i> have outsold the first week sales totals of Guns N' Roses' two albums.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> 50 Cent showed graciousness in regards to his defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-Weigh_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weigh-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> In a statement released to the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a>, he said, "I am very excited to have participated in one of the biggest album release weeks in the last two years. Collectively, we have sold hundreds of thousands of units in our debut week. This marks a great moment for hip-hop music, one that will go down in history."<sup id="cite_ref-Weigh_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weigh-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> After years of slumping sales, the album competition between the two releases and the resulting record breaking performances both albums demonstrated was considered to be a "fantastic day for hip-hop."<sup id="cite_ref-Rodriguez_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In its second week on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, <i>Graduation</i> slid to number two with the release of <a href="/wiki/Reba_McEntire" title="Reba McEntire">Reba McEntire</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Reba:_Duets" title="Reba: Duets">Reba: Duets</a></i>, selling 226,000 copies while maintaining its dominance over <i>Curtis</i>, which sold 143,000.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> The next week, with the releases of over 40 new albums, <i>Graduation</i> dropped three spaces to number five and registered 133,300, reaching a cumulative total of 1.3 million copies by October 3.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Selling 92,400 copies, the album descended two spots the following week to reach number seven.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> During its fourth week on the chart, <i>Graduation</i> experienced a slight rebound and rose from number seven to six on October 17, selling 71,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> The following week, the album began to descend once more, selling an estimated 54,000 copies and dropping three places to reach the ninth position on October 24.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> By year's end, <i>Graduation</i> was the third most-downloaded and best-selling album of 2007 on <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Graduation</i> became West's third consecutive studio album to sell over two million copies in the United States, and it was certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">double platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA) on October 18, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-riaa_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riaa-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> As of June 14, 2013, Nielsen Soundscan reported that <i>Graduation</i> has since grossed over 2,700,000 copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<th scope="col">Rating</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic" class="mw-redirect">Allmusic</a></td>

srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110" /><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" <tr>
<td scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a></td>
<td style="vertical-align:middle"><span style="white-space:nowrap" title="3/5 stars"><img alt="3/5 stars" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x,
