srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110" /><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110" /><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/17px-Star_empty.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110" /><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/17px-Star_empty.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110" /></span><sup id="cite_ref-Henderson_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Henderson-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i></td>
<td style="vertical-align:middle">8/10<sup id="cite_ref-Aaron_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aaron-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>Graduation</i> received generally positive reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a>. At <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a href="/wiki/Standard_score" title="Standard score">normalized</a> rating out of 100 to reviews from mainstream critics, the album received an <a href="/wiki/Weighted_mean" title="Weighted mean" class="mw-redirect">average</a> score of 79, based on 32 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic" class="mw-redirect">Allmusic</a>'s Andy Kellman credited West for "being his shrewd, occasionally foolish, and adventurous self", and stated, "Those who have admired Kanye as a sharp producer while detesting him as an inept <a href="/wiki/Master_of_ceremonies" title="Master of ceremonies">MC</a> might find the gleaming synth sprites ... to be one of the most glaring deal-breakers in hip-hop history."<sup id="cite_ref-Kellman_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kellman-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" title="Pitchfork Media">Pitchfork Media</a>'s Mark Pytlik complimented the accessibility of West's sonic experimentation, noting his visionary proficiency with interweaving seeminly disparate elements and bridging musical gaps.<sup id="cite_ref-Pytlik_46-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pytlik-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Greg_Tate" title="Greg Tate">Greg Tate</a>, writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i>, dubbed him "the most genuinely confessional MC in hip-hop today" and said, "bouts of narcissism aside, <i>Graduation</i> contains killer pieces of production."<sup id="cite_ref-Tate_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tate-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i> called the album "mesmerizing and alienating, like all the purest forms of <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture" title="Popular culture">pop culture</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-Aaron_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aaron-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stylus_Magazine" title="Stylus Magazine">Stylus Magazine</a>'s Jayson Greene said that it "serves as a document of West's maturation" and, "musically, at least, it's the most accomplished thing he's ever done."<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In his review for <i>Rolling Stone</i>, <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Brackett" title="Nathan Brackett">Nathan Brackett</a> complimented the continuously evolving and increasingly <a href="/wiki/Experimental_music" title="Experimental music">experimental</a>, genre-bending sonancy of West's production and said that, although he lacks Jay-Z's "formal mastery," West has "grown as a writer ... and given the lousy year hip-hop has had, the music needs his spazzed-out, neurotic creativity more than ever."<sup id="cite_ref-Brackett_50-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brackett-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Josh_Tyrangiel" title="Josh Tyrangiel">Josh Tyrangiel</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> wrote, "Thin as <i>Graduation</i> is on material, it delivers knockout hooks at a <a href="/wiki/Louis_Vuitton" title="Louis Vuitton">Louis Vuitton</a> price point... West plunders the best and meticulously layers every track with enough surprises that there are thrills and discoveries a dozen listens in."<sup id="cite_ref-Tyrangiel_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tyrangiel-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> Dorian Lynskey of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> felt that, despite occasionally disappointing lyrics, West generally "undercuts rap cliches with wit and ambivalence."<sup id="cite_ref-Lynskey_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lynskey-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MSN_Music" title="MSN Music">MSN Music</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a> commented that "every single track offers up its momentary pleasures—choruses that make you say yeah on songs you've already found wanting, confessional details and emotional <a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aper%C3%A7us" class="extiw" title="wikt:aperçus">aperçus</a> on an album that still reduces to quality product when they're over."<sup id="cite_ref-Christgau_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christgau-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ann_Powers" title="Ann Powers">Ann Powers</a>, writing in the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i>, interpreted the album's subtly dark tone to be the byproduct of the inevitable toil on West after revitalizing hip-hop as a genre:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p><i>Graduation</i><span style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s intricate musical environments take a while to comprehend, and at times they seem at odds with West's confrontational lyrics. But this contradictory music makes sense when heard as an attempt to express an internal struggle – between the Kanye West hip-hop made and the West who can't be contained by it or any other genre. It's hard to stop running with the crowd, even for a trendsetter. But West is on the verge, and moving forward ... a joker who couldn't be more serious, displaced and mobile because of race instead of class and an innovator in a genre that he must at least partially destroy to renew.<sup id="cite_ref-Powers_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Powers-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In a mixed review, <a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a>'s Eric Henderson found West's lyrics "only transparently expressive" and said that the songs' hooks "grab your ear on the first listen (notably bypassing your brain), your balls on the second, and your soul from there on out."<sup id="cite_ref-Henderson_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Henderson-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Dave Heaton of <a href="/wiki/PopMatters" title="PopMatters">PopMatters</a> felt that the album is ordinary and lacks the epochal feel of <i>Late Registration</i>, with songs that "aren't as richly dressed, and he doesn't seem to be trying as hard."<sup id="cite_ref-Heaton_56-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heaton-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i><span style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Neil Drumming found the album's music "uninspiring" and commented that "West's vocal mediocrity wouldn't be so glaring if the production were more of a diversion."<sup id="cite_ref-Drumming_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Drumming-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jon_Pareles" title="Jon Pareles">Jon Pareles</a>, writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, observed "some clever rhymes" in West's fame-obsessed lyrics and stated, "where he used to identify with everyday dreamers and strivers, now he seems happy to stay in his V.I.P. zone: all dressed up and behind that velvet rope."<sup id="cite_ref-Pareles_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pareles-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Rolling Stone</i> placed the album at number five on its list of their Top 50 Albums of 2007."<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Graduation</i> was listed at number nine on the <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> Critics' Poll.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> listed <i>Graduation</i> as the tenth best album of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-Tyrangiel_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tyrangiel-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> A year-end poll conducted by <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> cited <i>Graduation</i> as the best album of 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> It was also hailed as the best album of the year by <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>, which wrote, "The Louis Vuitton Don may major in rap, but he liberally borrows from other music schools to create a much broader soundscape."<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was listed as the fourth and eighteenth best record of the year by <i>Spin</i> magazine and Pitchfork Media respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/PopMatters" title="PopMatters">PopMatters</a> also listed <i>Graduation</i> as the fourth best album of the year."<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Graduation</i> was listed at number thirty-five by <i>The Observer</i> on its best fifty albums of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> ranked it number fifteen on its list of "Pop CDs of the Year," writing, "Kanye West finally grew up on this album, delivering more inventive, precision-tooled hip-hop but wearing a much more furrowed brow as he explored his existential anxieties. Dark and addictive."<sup id="cite_ref-PopCD_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopCD-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitchfork Media placed <i>Graduation</i> at number 87 on their list of top 200 albums of the 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Graduation</i> was cited as the second best album of the entire decade by <i><a href="/wiki/Complex_(magazine)" title="Complex (magazine)">Complex</a></i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/50th_Grammy_Awards" title="50th Grammy Awards" class="mw-redirect">50th Grammy Awards</a>, West led the field with a total of eight nominations, including <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a>, <a href="/wiki/Best_Rap/Sung_Collaboration" title="Best Rap/Sung Collaboration" class="mw-redirect">Best Rap/Sung Collaboration</a> for "Good Life", and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Song" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Song">Best Rap Song</a> for "Can't Tell Me Nothing".<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> He won the Grammy awards for <a href="/wiki/Best_Rap_Solo_Performance" title="Best Rap Solo Performance" class="mw-redirect">Best Rap Solo Performance</a> for "Stronger", Best Rap Song for "Good Life", and finally <i>Graduation</i> received the award for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> At the 34th annual <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards" class="mw-redirect">American Music Awards</a>, West received the awards for Favorite Rap/Hip-Hop Male Artist as well as Favorite Rap/Hip-Hop Album for <i>Graduation</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> However, West offered the former to Lil Wayne, who he felt was more deserving of the award due to his musical efforts in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> Praising the artistry expressed by <i>Graduation</i>, the success of the album's singles, and the imagination of its accompanying international <a href="/wiki/Glow_in_the_Dark_Tour" title="Glow in the Dark Tour">Glow in the Dark Tour</a>, MTV crowned West as the year's #1 <a href="/wiki/Hottest_MC_in_the_Game" title="Hottest MC in the Game" class="mw-redirect">Hottest MC in the Game</a> on May 16, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy_and_influence">Legacy and influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Legacy and influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kanye_West_Chicago_Tour_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a1/Kanye_West_Chicago_Tour_2008.jpg/240px-Kanye_West_Chicago_Tour_2008.jpg" width="240" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a1/Kanye_West_Chicago_Tour_2008.jpg/360px-Kanye_West_Chicago_Tour_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a1/Kanye_West_Chicago_Tour_2008.jpg/480px-Kanye_West_Chicago_Tour_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3552" data-file-height="2368" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kanye_West_Chicago_Tour_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf6/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
West performing at the <a href="/wiki/United_Center" title="United Center">United Center</a> in Chicago on the <a href="/wiki/Glow_in_the_Dark_Tour" title="Glow in the Dark Tour">supporting tour</a> for <i>Graduation</i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Irish rock band <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> has asserted that touring with West on their Vertigo Tour had a significant effect on their own music as well in regards to their twelfth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/No_Line_on_the_Horizon" title="No Line on the Horizon">No Line on the Horizon</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Calloway_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calloway-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> Bono elaborated that West's rapping inspired him to utilize more percussive consonants for his songwriting and vocal performance.<sup id="cite_ref-Calloway_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calloway-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> West's third studio album <i>Graduation</i>, particularly with its two hit singles "Stronger" and "Flashing Lights", has been accredited to not only encouraging other hip-hop artists to incorporate <a href="/wiki/House_(music)" title="House (music)" class="mw-redirect">house</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electronica" title="Electronica">electronica</a> elements into their music, but also for playing a part in the <a href="/wiki/Synthpop#21st_century_revival" title="Synthpop">revival</a> of <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electro_music" title="Electro music" class="mw-redirect">electro</a>-infused music in the late 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, tracks such as "Everything I Am" have been cited as "the best example of the soulful and introspective atmosphere that came to dominate the rap world, from <a href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" title="Drake (entertainer)" class="mw-redirect">Drake</a> to <a href="/wiki/The_Weeknd" title="The Weeknd">The Weeknd</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-Poll_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poll-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> West has also received praise for his managing to appeal to diverse music audiences such as <a href="/wiki/Indie_rock" title="Indie rock">indie-rock</a> listeners and <a href="/wiki/Rave_music" title="Rave music">rave</a> enthusiasts all without alienating his core hip-hop audiences.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ben Detrick of <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL</a></i> cited the outcome of the sales competition between 50 Cent's <i>Curtis</i> and West's <i>Graduation</i> as being responsible for altering the direction of hip-hop and paving the way for new rappers who didn't follow the <a href="/wiki/Hardcore_hip_hop" title="Hardcore hip hop">hardcore</a>-<a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangster</a> mold, writing, "If there was ever a <a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/watershed" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:watershed">watershed</a> moment to indicate hip-hop's changing direction, it may have come when 50 Cent competed with Kanye in 2007 to see whose album would claim superior sales. 50 lost handily, and it was made clear that excellent songcrafting trumped a lack of street-life experience. Kanye led a wave of new artists—<a href="/wiki/Kid_Cudi" title="Kid Cudi">Kid Cudi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wale_(rapper)" title="Wale (rapper)">Wale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lupe_Fiasco" title="Lupe Fiasco">Lupe Fiasco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kidz_in_the_Hall" title="Kidz in the Hall">Kidz in the Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" title="Drake (entertainer)" class="mw-redirect">Drake</a>—who lacked the interest or ability to create narratives about any past gunplay or <a href="/wiki/Drug-dealing" title="Drug-dealing" class="mw-redirect">drug-dealing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-XXL_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XXL-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> Similarly, in a retrospective article, Rosie Swash of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> viewed the competition between 50 Cent and Kanye West as a historical moment in hip-hop, writing that it "highlighted the diverging facets of hip-hop in the last decade; the former was gangsta rap for the noughties, while West was the thinking man's alternative.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<dt><b>Notes:</b><sup id="cite_ref-linernotes_18-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linernotes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>"Good Morning" contains samples of "<a href="/wiki/Someone_Saved_My_Life_Tonight" title="Someone Saved My Life Tonight">Someone Saved My Life Tonight</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a></li>
<li>"Champion" contains elements of "<a href="/wiki/Kid_Charlemagne" title="Kid Charlemagne">Kid Charlemagne</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Steely_Dan" title="Steely Dan">Steely Dan</a></li>
<li>"Stronger" contains samples of "<a href="/wiki/Harder,_Better,_Faster,_Stronger" title="Harder, Better, Faster, Stronger">Harder, Better, Faster, Stronger</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Daft_Punk" title="Daft Punk">Daft Punk</a></li>
<li>"I Wonder" contains samples of "My Song" by <a href="/wiki/Labi_Siffre" title="Labi Siffre">Labi Siffre</a></li>
<li>"Good Life" contains samples of "<a href="/wiki/P.Y.T._(Pretty_Young_Thing)" title="P.Y.T. (Pretty Young Thing)">P.Y.T. (Pretty Young Thing)</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a></li>
<li>"Barry Bonds" contains samples of "Long Red" by <a href="/wiki/Mountain_(band)" title="Mountain (band)">Mountain</a></li>
<li>"Drunk and Hot Girls" contains elements of "Sing Swan Song" performed by <a href="/wiki/Can_(band)" title="Can (band)">Can</a></li>
<li>"Everything I Am" contains elements of "If We Can't Be Lovers" by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Phillip_Mitchell" title="Prince Phillip Mitchell" class="mw-redirect">Prince Phillip Mitchell</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Bring_the_Noise" title="Bring the Noise">Bring the Noise</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Public_Enemy_(band)" title="Public Enemy (band)" class="mw-redirect">Public Enemy</a></li>
<li>"The Glory" contains samples of "Save the Country" by <a href="/wiki/Laura_Nyro" title="Laura Nyro">Laura Nyro</a>, "Long Red" by Mountain</li>
<li>"Good Night" contains samples of "Nuff Man a Dead" by <a href="/wiki/Super_Cat" title="Super Cat">Super Cat</a>, "Wake The Town" by <a href="/wiki/U-Roy" title="U-Roy">U-Roy</a></li>
<li>"Bittersweet Poetry" interpolates "Bittersweet" by <a href="/wiki/Chairmen_of_the_Board" title="Chairmen of the Board">Chairmen of the Board</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel">Personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduation_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Credits adapted from <a href="/wiki/Liner_notes" title="Liner notes">liner notes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-linernotes_18-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linernotes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
<tr>
<td style="width:50%; text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<ul>
